<div id="theReview">
<h2>Snowtown</h2>
<p class="ratd"> Rated <em>MA</em></p>
<p><em>Review by Margaret Pomeranz</em></p>
<p>SNOWTOWN is one of four Australian presences at the Cannes Film Festival this year, it has been selected for Critics Week, quite an achievement for director Justin Kurzel. His debut feature charts the terrible loss of innocence of Jamie Vlassakis, LUCAS PITTAWAY, as Jamie comes under the spell of the notorious serial killer John Bunting, DANIEL HENSHALL. <br/><br/>Set in the outer northern suburbs of Adelaide where the real murders actually took place, it is a world of bleakness and fanatacism where neighbours gather to vent their spleen against the people they see as perverts in their midst.<br/><br/>It is a relentlessly chilling experience as Jamie is exposed to the real evil that lurks in Bunting's heart.<br/><br/>There is no doubting Justin Kurzel's talent for creating a believable world on screen. And his performers, many of them non-professional deliver. DANIEL HENSHALL especially gives a tremendously brave performance as Bunting. Whether it is a world that many of us would want to venture into is another question because Kurzel does not pull back from exposing the audience to some of the grotesque brutality perpetrated by Bunting and his cohorts. <br/><br/>Some scenes are very hard to sit through. It's a confusing world, with relationships not easy to track. But the sheer banality of the background against which these horrific crimes were carried out is eye-opening. Bunting's insistence on being the cook, feeding this family that he has inveigled his way into is deeply disconcerting. <br/><br/>If we the audience are looking for a moral centre of the film in Jamie then we are doomed to disappointment, and that is one of the problems. The moral centre lies with us in the audience, on screen there is only madness.</p>
<h2>Further comments</h2>
<p>MARGARET: David?<br/><br/>DAVID: It's interesting because a couple of weeks ago when we talked about MAD BASTARDS, I was saying that some Australian films don't seem to know how to start. They don't know how to sort of set up the characters and the place where the story is taking place or they take so long to establish it that there's too much confusion in the minds of the audience. This is a very good example of that problem in Australian films, I think, because in the early scenes of this I had no idea what relationship people were to one another, the geography of the area.<br/> <br/>MARGARET: Yes. No, I agree with you.<br/><br/>DAVID: It was too confusing for too long and, again, as I said before, I think sometimes filmmakers have got to step back. They know what it's all about. We don't and they have to step back and look at it with a stranger's eye and say does this make sense? Having said that, though, I think the performances in this film are amazing; absolutely amazing.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Yes.<br/><br/>DAVID: And once I got into the film, I found it exerted a very dark power over me.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Yes, it does.<br/><br/>DAVID: It is pretty confronting.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, that's what I felt. I think that, if a film can grab you, regardless of confusion about location and relationships at the start and just sort of like drag you literally by the throat through this experience, it's quite an achievement and Pittaway is just fantastic for a kid from a mall. They found him in a mall. He'd never done anything before.<br/><br/>DAVID: The performances are amazing but if you compare this to, say, ANIMAL KINGDOM, which is not that dissimilar in some elements, that was a beautifully made, crystal clear film and this one suffers by comparison somewhat, I think.<br/><br/>MARGARET: That was Shakespearean. This is really almost a documentary in a lot of ways.<br/><br/>DAVID: Yes, sure. Okay. <br/><br/>MARGARET: So, look I'm giving it three and a half stars. I think it's got its faults but I think it's very strong.<br/><br/>DAVID: I'm giving it three.</p>

<h3>beth :</h3>
<p class="date">29 Nov 2013 11:42:49pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[3]]<br>I resisted watching this film for a long time because I could not see the merit in glorifying the murderers who, because of court suppression orders, were largely unknown. But after reading positive reviews I decided to watch it with an open mind. Yes, the direction, performances and soundtrack are very strong but I remain unconvinced that, of all the stories in the world, THIS was the one that needed to be told.</br></p>

Their reason; to avenge the killing of Muslims in Iraq and Afghanistan by foreign troops.<br>The film made me think more about extremism in all different cultures, now and in the past, and how one self appointed, self righteous maniac can so easily manipulate the most  vulnerable people  to commit the most terrible acts.</br></br></br></p>

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay22087_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m22087"></a>
<h3>taipan :</h3>
<p class="date">26 May 2013 6:59:49am</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[10]]<br>I didn't experience any confusion at the start. Anyone like me who has experienced urban wastelands like this would find all the characters credible. Excellent sound track as well, and the acting was extremely accurate. We shouldn't shy away from what we are, an occasionally primitive society hiding all sorts of loonies in our midst. Art is about honesty, so let's have no more  sanitised 'Animal Kingdom' movies please! And no silly horror films like 'Wolf Creek'. The film reminded me of 'Wake in Fright'. It had that same nightmarish quality and brilliant acting.</br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=22087&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d273%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>arnie :</h3>
<p class="date">27 Mar 2013 11:38:18am</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[10]]<br>Brilliant,brutal...The best Australian film of 2011. There was so much controversy about the making of this film in terms of the victims families having to experience the horror all over again..The pressure was on the filmakers to make it honestly but not gratuitously..They certainly succeeded..The portrayal of Bunting was chillingly evil and the ensemble of first time actors gave this film and the viewer a sense of reality...not for the squeamish as the subject matter is so intensely sordid and dark..This film haunts..and to think it was based on fact again says much about the darkside of our society.</br></p>

<li>
<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay20219_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m20219"></a>
<h3>Mr_Right :</h3>
<p class="date">20 Feb 2013 10:34:03pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[10]]<br>I actually LIKED what others call the "confusion" aspect. Yes, characters wander in &amp; out mumbling at one another in thick dialect without traditional introductions or explanations of their relationships-just as if we secretly observed any real-life group of strangers. This organic, immersive approach to storytelling contributes to an overwhelming realism.<br><br>All but one of the many murders occur offscreen, so when we finally witness the full repugnant truth of the depravity we've been suspecting, it's heartstopping, nauseating, and perfect. <br><br>Not for all tastes, but a magnificent film. BTW, I had no idea it was a true story until afterward.</br></br></br></br></br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=20219&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d273%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<li>
<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay18570_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m18570"></a>
<h3>Dan :</h3>
<p class="date">14 Nov 2012 4:00:39pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[9]]<br>I was stunned by this film. Margaret &amp; David, you speak of context. If you've ever lived in Adelaide, ever visited Salisbury or Elizabeth, you'd know exactly who these people are immediately, their environment, their mannerisms, everything. This film was just absolutely spot on. The banality, the depression, the isolation, the complete introversion, it was all accurately, frighteningly portrayed. Not easily realized when you're accustomed to the friendly openness and opportunity afforded most of Australia. It takes bravery and real vision to shine a light into the darkest recesses of society, and this film offers a rare, unflinching insight.</br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=18570&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d273%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>STM :</h3>
<p class="date">18 Jul 2012 12:58:45am</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[9]]<br>I didn't feel like it was about the snowtown murders, more like it could happen anywhere anytime which made it chilling. Rather being put off by the lose story the caracters were so compelling I stopped caring about the details. Difficult to watch but also humane and lifelike in its portrayal of the characters. The DVD commentary is revealing with discussions on the artistic choices and background on the people portrayed. The usual judging criteria for film doesn't do it justice, it's a great example of how a film can be more than just a film.</br></p>

<h3>BJM :</h3>
<p class="date">18 Jun 2012 11:44:56pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[5]]<br>I live in Snowtown, so possibly I had more of an interest to know what these murders were all about (I think), &amp; partly they were about Centrelink Fraud, which I didn't see any evidence of in this movie, apart from a wallet being wanted at one time. The movie was very well acted, but sometimes it was difficult to know what was being said, as there was some mumbling. I guess it's the sort of story where there just isn't enough time to cover all of the specifics, which I found disappointing. Not much about bodies in barrels, either.</br></p>

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay15418_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m15418"></a>
<h3>worrierqueen :</h3>
<p class="date">03 Jun 2012 1:56:59pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[7]]<br>The Australian posed a question, why do we know the name Milat but not Bunting? The reason being that Bunting's motivation (which is explored in the film) is ostensibly due to his hatred of child molestors, and what he says is what you hear around many BBQs ("killing's too good for them"). Bunting just acts it out.<br><br>Absolutely chilling film of horror, hopelessness and helplessness in the burbs. Wouldn't dream of taking my children, wouldn't see again, but its the sort of film, once seen, you don't forget in a hurry.</br></br></br></p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=15418&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d273%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>tracy :</h3>
<p class="date">08 Mar 2012 3:56:04pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[9]]<br>I was riveted! The way the poverty and depressing lifestyle was portrayed was spot-on - I could  smell the musty mattresses and mouldy rooms. Rubbish laying around the backyards, the cheap pasta served up night after night, playing pokies for entertainment,  the single mum struggling to raise three boys, sexual abuse .....all of this made the scenario of John Bunting worming his way into their lives and taking over completely plausible.  Daniel Henshall jumps out from the screen.I had little trouble figuring out relationships...and those who were a bit of a mystery eventually become clear - or it didn't matter.</br></p>

<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[0]]<br>Astounding acting, superb crafting of a morally bankrupt, appalling story. It's deeply disturbing that sanity did not prevail and the project was stopped. <p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[10]]<br/>One of the best Australian movies. (I'd almost given up!)  I much preferred it to the more commercial Animal Kingdom.  The actors were superb. <h3>Kaite :</h3>
<p class="date">06 Jun 2011 10:34:08am</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[8]]<br/>A well done film, which was more real than Animal Kingdom. The violence was pretty intense, however it wasn't gratuitously depicted, given the actual events which took place. The film also dealt sensitively with its subjects and showed how easy it was for people to be exploited and abused in such a disadvantaged environment. <h3>Leigh :</h3>
<p class="date">04 Jun 2011 3:35:41pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[8]]<br/>Director Justin Kurzel has achieved some incredible factors with Snowtown. The performances he has guided from an amateur, unknown cast are exemplary! Daniel Henshall's portrayal of Bunting is deserving of the male equivalent nomination Weaver received for Animal Kingdom last year! A naturalistic sense of place and being are strongly seen and felt in Snowtown due to the skilful cinematography by Animal Kingdom's Adam Arkapaw and a hypnotic score from the sound department. A notable direction flaw that causes confusion and slightly prolongs the second half doesn't cause too much damage to the insurmountable tension and unforgettable final scene.</p>

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay7700_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m7700"></a>
<h3>Ryan James :</h3>
<p class="date">26 May 2011 4:15:47pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[10]]<br/>Anyone who says this film isn't perfect is incorrect.  It is difficult to make sense of what is going and what the character's motivations are. That's the point; you are thrust into this world, struggling to make sense of it morally. Initially, you're somewhat complicit in Bunting's schemes (I enjoyed watching him stand up to the pedophile across the street) and it is difficult to pinpoint exactly where you depart from this. I suspect this is the true reason that this makes some people feel uncomfortable and reject this film. However, it is also the film's true value and power.</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=7700&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d273%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

<h3>Noel Hodda :</h3>
<p class="date">25 May 2011 10:31:46am</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[7]]<br/>I have been pondering this film since I saw it and I have come to the conclusion that it is important. These people exist and we, as members of society, need to know and see that. We need to know what society such people can be borne from. Seeing the police investigation and capture, as some have called for here, is pointless. We know that happened. What the film makers have concerned themselves with are the causes - the breeding ground for this violence. This is not The Boys nor Animal Kingdom. It is darker and more honest.</p>

<h3>Chris :</h3>
<p class="date">23 May 2011 8:57:00pm</p>
<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[9]]<br/>Yes, it is gruelling and intense.  And so it should be, given the subject matter.  If you don't like films that take you to an uncomfortable edge (I think David Stratton is in this category), then don't watch this.  It will be compared to Animal Kingdom, which presented a heavily sanitised version of the characters and events on which it was inspired.  However, Snowtown pays great respect to the real life events and is a superb achievement.  Not an enjoyable film, but very impressive nonetheless.</p>

<p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[8]]<br/>The film is well made but almost unbearable to watch because of its unremitting depiction of  Bunting's psychopathic mind, the implied violence in the film (which paradoxically made it worse), the social wasteland, which provided the context in which the behaviour was allowed to flourish, and the amorality of  those depressingly disadvantaged individuals who were so easily co-opted to participate in the killings. <br/><br/>I walked out for a brief period and had to grit my teeth to see the rest of it. <p class="comment">((Snowtown))[[10]]<br/>A masterpiece.<br/><br/>It's true that the expectation here is that the audience will keep up with a story told in fragments which don't really start to to come together for some time, but I think this is actually helpful. <script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">


var newtopicKey;

$(document).ready(function(){

audShow();
changeAction();
formatComments();

// end ready
});	

function audShow() {
	// display word count only if js enabled
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='inline';
	document.getElementById("audiencecomment").style.display='block';
	if (document.getElementById("allnewComments")) {
		document.getElementById("allnewComments").innerHTML = document.getElementById("loadComments").innerHTML;
	}
}


function changeAction() {
	// avoids non-js form submission 
	var tmpStoryid = "??StoryID??";
	if (document.m_frmMainForm) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/NewMessage.aspx?b=117&amp;tn='+tmpStoryid+'&amp;dm=1&amp;tpa=&amp;r=&amp;layout=popup';
		}
}



function formatComments() {
	// replace H3 tag with 'Name:' + name
	var arrayH3 = document.getElementById("comments").getElementsByTagName("h3");
	for (var i = 0; i < arrayH3.length; i++) {
		var theString = arrayH3[i].innerHTML;
		theString = theString.replace(":", "");
		theString = "Name: "+theString;
		arrayH3[i].innerHTML = 	theString;
	}
	// add rating value to each comment
	var arrayComment = getElementsByClassName( 'comment', 'p' );	
	for (var c = 0; c < arrayComment.length; c++) {
		var theComment = arrayComment[c].innerHTML;
		theComment = theComment.replace("[[", "<span class='userRating'>Rating: <img src='https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/stars").replace("]]",".png' alt='rating'></span>").replace("((", "<!-- ").replace(")))", "))").replace("))", "-->");
		arrayComment[c].innerHTML = theComment;
	}

	
}


function formCheck(zeForm) {
	// pass key to form
	document.getElementById("keyField").value = newtopicKey;
	// basic validation
	if (document.getElementById("yname").value.length < 1) {
		alert("Please enter your name or nickname.");
		document.getElementById("yname").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (document.getElementById("yemail").value.length < 6) {
		alert("Please enter a valid email address.");
		document.getElementById("yemail").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (zeForm.score.options[0].selected && zeForm.score.options[0].value=="na") {
		alert("You forgot to rate the movie!");
		document.getElementById("score").style.background='#FFFDC8';	
		return false;
	}	
	// check for http
	spamcheck=zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	if (spamcheck.indexOf("http")!=-1) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141229135742/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/blank.htm';
	}
	// check word count
	wct = cnt(zeForm.m_tbxText.value);
	if (wct > 100) {
		alert("Comments are limited to 100 words. You've written "+wct+" words!");
		document.getElementById("remark").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;	
	}
	
	// replace usual suspect bad characters 
	badChars = Array  ('', '', '', '', '', 'ö', 'é', 'è', 'ñ', 'â', ' ', '','','´');
	goodChars = Array ('...', '-', '-', '"', '"', 'o', 'e', 'e', 'n', 'a', ' ', '\'','\'','\'');
	fld = document.getElementById("remark");
	for(i=0;i<badChars.length;i++){
		restring = new RegExp( badChars[i] , 'g');
		fld.value = fld.value.replace(restring,goodChars[i]);
	}
	fldn = document.getElementById("yname");
	for(j=0;j<badChars.length;j++){
		restringj = new RegExp( badChars[j] , 'g');
		fldn.value = fldn.value.replace(restringj,goodChars[j]);
	}	
	
	// add rating to comment field in [[ ]] tags 
	var theSel = zeForm.score.selectedIndex;
	var theRating = zeForm.score[theSel].value; 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "[["+theRating+"]]\n" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	
	// add movie title to comment field in (( )) tags 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "(("+theMovie+"))" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;	
	
	// display thankyou div layer and hide form. 
	document.getElementById("favFormThx").style.display='block';
	document.getElementById("favForm").style.display='none';
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='none';	
	
	// all clear, submit the form
	return true;
}

// word count function
function cnt(theform){
	var y=theform;
	var r = 0;
	a=y.replace('\n',' ');
	a=a.split(' ');
	for (z=0; z<a.length; z++) {if (a[z].length > 0) r++;}
	return r;
}

function remainingWords(textAreaContent,textAreaContentValue, maxWords) 
{
	// Determine the number of words we have left
	var numberofwords = cnt(textAreaContentValue);
	wordsLeft = maxWords - numberofwords;
	if (wordsLeft < 1)
	{	// if 100 change color to red
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='red'; 
	} else {
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='#ffffff'; 
	}
	// update word count number
	document.getElementById("wcNum").innerHTML=(0+numberofwords);
}

// windows media alt box
function showWindows() {
	document.getElementById("windowsMed").style.display='block';
}


// generic get by class name
function getElementsByClassName(strClass, strTag, objContElm) {
  strTag = strTag || "*";
  objContElm = objContElm || document;    
  var objColl = objContElm.getElementsByTagName(strTag);
  if (!objColl.length &&  strTag == "*" &&  objContElm.all) objColl = objContElm.all;
  var arr = new Array();                              
  var delim = strClass.indexOf('|') != -1  ? '|' : ' ';   
  var arrClass = strClass.split(delim);    
  for (var i = 0, j = objColl.length; i < j; i++) {                         
    var arrObjClass = objColl[i].className.split(' ');   
    if (delim == ' ' && arrClass.length > arrObjClass.length) continue;
    var c = 0;
    comparisonLoop:
    for (var k = 0, l = arrObjClass.length; k < l; k++) {
      for (var m = 0, n = arrClass.length; m < n; m++) {
        if (arrClass[m] == arrObjClass[k]) c++;
        if ((delim == '|' && c == 1) || (delim == ' ' && c == arrClass.length)) {
          arr.push(objColl[i]); 
          break comparisonLoop;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return arr; 
}

	newtopicKey = theKey;
}
